< review>
I walked in earlier this afternoon to the facility in San Pedro with a friend looking for a unit to rent out. I'm not from LA so I was skeptical on what I could find to hold my things for a reasonable price.  We were promptly addressed by a woman named Carla at the counter. She was genuine in her greeting and insisted that had there been any questions that arose that we not hesitate to ask. We had been to other facilities but seeing as this was a pretty big store we had asked if we could take a look at one of the units, hence I wasn't too sure if I was ready to rent one at this facility or even rent a unit at all. Carla was able to relate to us on a personal level and kept her explanations short and to the point. Since I'm from Alaska, I was planning on transitioning over to LA but wanted to make sure I had everything in check for myself. I also was a bit worried with what I need such as extra boxes. Carla reassured me that they happen to have boxes at a decent price as well if I happened to run into trouble needing things to make the haul of the load somewhat better. Carla was very knowledgeable, respectable, helpful, kind, genuine, and not to mention hilarious. Not only did she have us to deal with but all the while busy with answering phone calls and other customers in such a professional manner. I was highly impressed with her talent for multitasking at such a quick pace, ( A comment my friend also mentioned to me) Her customer service was pure excellence. It's very rare to find great customer service like hers where everything just flows naturally. When we were finished with our visit Carla walked us out the store with such a warm smile and ended the day with mentioning how their doors would always be open to us if there were anymore questions or interests. Thanks to Carla and her wonderful service, she's made my decision on moving to LA a quick and easy one especially on where to rent out a space and given me the influence to constantly return to the facility and to share it with many other people. Thanks Carla so much, you're awesome :)</review>

< review>
I went to Monkey Sports to buy new ice skates. The salesman who helped me was very friendly and accommodating. I tried on several pairs of skates before settling on the Vapor X7.0. I asked the salesman if Monkey Sports offered free skate sharpening for the life of the skates if I bought the skates there (Hockey Giant offers this service).  He said yes, so I got the skates baked, I paid and left.

I came back about a week later to get the skates sharpened and was asked to pay $6 at the counter. I questioned the cashier's reason for charging me and explained that the salesman promised me free skate sharpening. She said, "No, we only sharpen them once when you first buy the skates."

The employee who sold me the skates happened to be working that day. I explained to him that I was being charged for skate sharpening. He offered to go speak with the manager about my situation. He returned a few minutes later only to confirm what the cashier had told me: basically, "sorry dude.  Buyer beware." I left the store quite frustrated.

About a month after my purchase, I wrote a polite letter to Monkey Sports management explaining what happened.  After a few weeks of no response, I sent an email to the address on their website.  They never replied to the letter or the email.

I have since replaced the Vapors with Supreme NXGs purchased at Hockey Giant.  The skates even came with a little HG sticker on the bottom of the boot that gives me free skate sharpening at Giant for the life of the skates.

Monkey Sports, you have made me a Hockey Giant customer for life.</review>

<Review>It's nice that Cal Poly students have access to a mini-market and can use meal credit at it. That's a luxury that many University students don't have. But for non-meal credit holding students, the market is kind of mediocre. Item selection is pretty good for a convenience store, but the prices between items vary drastically. For instance, a small bag of "premium" trail mix costs $7.50 while a large bag of generic trail mix costs $2.99 ü§∑‚Äç‚ôÇÔ∏è. Ethan Zimbelman<//user_name>
< rating>
5</rating>
<time>1616806352150<//time><resp>{'time': 1617389358648, 'text': 'We‚Äôre thrilled you enjoyed our Campus Market Loaded Baked Potato (TM), we like making our customers happy at Campus Market!'}</resp>< Review>
BEST POTATOES ON THE PLANET. You definitely want to make your way to Campus Market between 11-3 on Monday and/or Tuesday to get a PREMIUM Campus Market Loaded Baked Potato (TM) for the price of one (1) meal credit. Options include a hot wing potato, which is definitely my personal favorite, BBQ, ranch-hand, and some other vegetarian option.

This is the absolute best usage of your time and money, so find a first year to plus daddy you if you don't have a meal plan. The only downside to this wonderful treat, is the fact that they are only served twice a week. This means the other 5 days, you're left wanting more. They have somewhat fixed this problem by serving rice bowls for lunch at the same time on Thursday and Friday, but this seems like an afterthought compared to the perfection that is the Campus Market Loaded Baked Potato (TM).

------

Outside of the Campus Market Loaded Baked Potato (TM), prices are ridiculously high and there isn't much room to actually eat your food if the weather is bad [something about always being sunny in SLO]. Normally, this would tank my rating, but the Campus Market Loaded Baked Potato (TM) is an absolute treat that keeps this rating at an unwavering 5 stars.</Review>

< Review>
I go to "Campus Markup" a lot solely because it is convenient and I'm on campus 10 hours a day. Almost everything is massively, frustratingly overpriced - it's a game for me at this point to find the most remote places in this country that are still cheaper than campus market. What's weird is that the price markups are inconsistent - you'll have candy that's the same price as off-campus next to peanut butter that's 3x its normal price.

The cooked food is pretty mediocre, and once again overpriced. I'd recommend the Starbucks breakfast sandwiches on the other side of the store over anything I've tried. The Starbucks, at least, is basically a normal Starbucks.

If you can go off campus, don't go here.</Review>

The prices are very high and are not listed for many items, making it very difficult to be a thrifty shopper. Also, the selection is rather small, and it is very difficult to find healthy food. < Text>
The Grill used to have decent food at an expensive price because it was at least made fresh to order, but now all you get is a dish that was half-assed and left under a heat lamp for 3 hours until you walked in the door. Seriously, the breakfast burrito went from halfway decent this past spring, to 90% uncooked tortilla and eggs week 1 of Fall 2017. Anything off of the Grill menu is worse now because it's basically cold and flavorless by the time you sit down to eat it AND with all of the renovations Poly has done, this farce of a meal is even more expensive than it was before. Salad bar is questionable on the best of days and the grocery items are (to put it lightly) marked up for convenience.
Students who work there are the saving grace because they at least have kind customer service manners and do their best given the work environment. I know that no one in administration takes these reviews seriously, but hopefully this will prevent someone else from getting scammed.
Cal Poly Corp, do better, because this is pathetic.</Text>

< Text>
An interesting take on Indian food, I was glad to have tried it although I'm not sure I would go back. Some of the dishes were great - the paneer Tikka sliders and fried cauliflower were good. The uni biryani rice looks impressive but isn't that great a dish. The dahl makhani was fine but not as tasty as many others I have had. The service was attentive, but the decor looks like it was a club in the 90s and hasn't been redesigned since. There are really not many vegetarian dishes, which is frustrating for an Indian restaurant in California!</Text>

<userid>117887271683918628365< /userid><user_name>Christopher Abatemarco<//user_name>< time>
1578210921408</time>
<Rating>2< /Rating>< text>
I honestly there's nothing truly awful here.
The service was acceptable, but not great.
The food was solid, but for such a limited menu and the price tag,  it should have been a contender for the best in Santa Barbara.
The atmosphere was trying to hard to be trendy and nightcluby, not to my liking, but that's just my taste, I don't dock them points here.

Of the wines I recognized, they were severally marked up from retail, and the $20 dollar corking fee makes it impossible to get a decent glass of wine here.

The beer, while competitively priced, was poorly displayed. There were no clear indicators to what types of beer they had. No tasting notes, no name plates, not even clear break down of types. From what I could tell they had IPAs and Saisons. While it was a wide selection within those categories, I felt it to be boring and uninspired, because they all seemed to flow together within the display.

All that being said, the real tragedy here is it seems like they have good ideas, but haven't taken the time to refine them or flesh them out. I hope they are able to really make the place shine.<//text>

< text>
Bibi Ji is the latest restaurant to occupy this location, and unfortunately, it misses the mark. I long for the days of Rudy's where locals and tourists alike were treated as respected guests of this establishment, but alas, new ownership has taken to create a hostile environment for its guests. A few things stood out as odd to me from reading the menu alone, details that I could not reconcile, and our "server" had difficulty answering. This is the kind of place that has many arbitrary rules, and hiked-up fees, purposefully confusing at best, pretentiousness more likely being the culprit of this self-described "unauthentic" Indian food restaurant. Soda: $5. Bread (naan): $5. Wine bottle: $40 to-go, $60 with meal ($20 corkage fee). Attitude from owner and server: FREE!</text>

<Text>One of our friends, a member of our wine tasting group of 7 couples, made reservations to this place upon recommendation of the restaurant's Sommelier co-owner.

This was much anticipated by all of us, as this was at the end of our amazing wine-tasting trip limited to Santa Barbara/Happy and Ballard Canyon region. This included brunch at the Four Seasons, and wine tasting at Crown Point and Kimsey's. Both vineyards were specially opened for our group on a Saturday by their respective owners as private events.

Upon arrival at the restaurant, the place appeared very small with a row of deuces facing a bar in the middle. Foursomes in the corners. A cooler for soft drinks/Beers was installed towards the back, a sight more typical for a fast-food place. We were then ushered to the back, which I assumed would be private room for 14 people, turned out to be an open EXIT concrete patio with barely two heaters. "Holy Grail" of Indian curries Or NOT. The place made other so called "Hole-in-the walls" look like Four Seasons.

Our lady server, who claimed to be the Chef's wife, appeared to be in a hurry. Never made us feel welcome, didn't tell us about the menus, didn't hand us out the menus and appeared Patronizing at best.

From then on the situation turned for the worse. Our friend asked the server if he could charge his discharged phone (the only phone that had the contact info of the Limo Driver), the server flatly refused. Our friend's wife then approached the Owner and explained the situation and that we would all have to leave if the phone remained discharged. He grudgingly agreed to charge the phone.

Server came back upset that we dared approach the manager, claiming that she never refused the phone charging to begin with!! A few minutes later the Owner came back and confronted my friend's wife aggressively saying that SHE had made the server cry!!!  When our friends tried to find an explanation for their rudeness and bizarre behavior, the Owner's response was "SO WHAT"!!!!

Suffice to say that we all left that place, despite the fact that our friend had pre-paid for the meal for the whole group. Couldn't Risk any further Disrespect and Insults for our well meaning Group.

Interesting at best. Service at worst. Wish we had read the reviews of this place prior to making the reservation. The common thread of the negative reviews were: Rude nonchalant service. Unresponsive Management. Over-priced Menu for a mediocre establishment and Poor Service.<//Text>< gmap_id>
